\section{Final Separation Between What Is Automatic in the Minimal Ansatz and What Must Be Verified in the Actual Microscopic TECT Realization}

\subsection{Goal}

The purpose of this section is to make a definitive separation between:

\begin{enumerate}
\item statements that are automatic inside the minimal shell-enriched projector ansatz;
\item statements that still require explicit verification in the actual microscopic TECT realization.
\end{enumerate}

This separation is essential.
At the present stage, the local shell-reduced fermion framework is already structurally closed, but the final microscopic realization is not yet fully verified.

Thus the correct logical status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local Weyl/Dirac architecture is closed at the minimal-ansatz level,}
}
\]
whereas
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic TECT realization still requires explicit finite checks.}
}
\]

\subsection{I. What is automatic in the minimal ansatz}

We first collect the statements that follow automatically once one adopts the minimal shell-enriched projector completion.

\subsubsection{1. Minimal condensate PDE class}

Under translation invariance, pre-condensation isotropy, finite-shell instability, and quartic stabilization, the minimal effective condensate PDE is of Landau--Brazovskii type:
\[
\partial_t\Phi
=
-r\Phi+\kappa\nabla^2\Phi-\lambda\nabla^4\Phi-u|\Phi|^2\Phi,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{\kappa}{2\lambda}.
\]
Thus the existence of a finite-shell instability and the corresponding BCC shell background are automatic at the minimal effective level.

\subsubsection{2. Allowed shell-enriched tensor space}

For the shell-relevant residual symmetry
\[
H_{\mathrm{sh}}=SO(2)_\perp,
\]
the allowed shell-relevant tensor space is exactly three-dimensional:
\[
V=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\]
Therefore none of the three shell-enriched channels is symmetry-forbidden:
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq0,
\qquad
P_VT^{(1)}\neq0,
\qquad
P_VT^{(2)}\neq0.
\]

\subsubsection{3. Explicit enriched tensor form}

The minimal shell-enriched projector coupling produces the explicit tensor triple
\[
N^3_{ij}=g_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
N^1_{ij}=g_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
\[
N^2_{ij}=g_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}.
\]
Thus the microscopic shell-enriched tensor structure is explicit in the minimal ansatz.

\subsubsection{4. Exact witness extraction}

The witness functionals
\[
W_\parallel,\qquad W_I,\qquad W_J
\]
are exactly dual to the invariant tensor basis and satisfy
\[
W_\parallel=g_\parallel,
\qquad
W_I=g_I,
\qquad
W_J=g_J.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
W_\parallel[N]=\hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij},
\]
\[
W_I[N]=\frac12
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}
\right),
\]
\[
W_J[N]=\frac12
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}-e_{2j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}
\right).
\]

\subsubsection{5. Local Weyl criterion}

In the minimal ansatz, the reduced Weyl coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_I,
\qquad
\beta=-\kappa_*|G_*|\,g_J,
\]
and therefore
\[
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3\,g_\parallel\,(g_I^2+g_J^2)
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3\,W_\parallel\,(W_I^2+W_J^2).
\]
Hence local Weyl nondegeneracy is automatic whenever
\[
g_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(g_I,g_J)\neq(0,0),
\]
or equivalently
\[
W_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(W_I,W_J)\neq(0,0).
\]

\subsubsection{6. Opposite-valley pairing in the minimal ansatz}

In the matched opposite-valley frame
\[
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_1^-=e_1^+,
\qquad
e_2^-=-e_2^+,
\]
the minimal ansatz uses the same three invariant coupling constants at \(\pm G_*\).
Therefore the witness triples satisfy
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+),
\]
and hence
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p).
\]
Thus local opposite-valley pairing is automatic in the minimal ansatz.

\subsubsection{7. Constant mass-space classification}

For the minimal doubled Dirac block
\[
H_D(q)=\rho^3\otimes(q_i\sigma^i),
\]
the constant Hermitian Dirac mass space is exactly
\[
\mathcal M
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho^1\otimes\mathbf 1,\,
\rho^2\otimes\mathbf 1
\}.
\]
Thus the mass problem is completely reduced to a finite \(4\times4\) matrix classification.

\subsection{II. What must still be verified in the actual microscopic TECT realization}

We now list the statements that do \emph{not} follow automatically from the minimal ansatz and must still be checked in the final microscopic model.

\subsubsection{1. Actual nonvanishing of the witness triple}

The minimal ansatz shows that the three channels are symmetry-allowed.
However, symmetry allowance does not imply actual nonvanishing.
In the full microscopic theory one must still verify that
\[
W_\parallel^\pm\neq0,
\qquad
(W_I^\pm,W_J^\pm)\neq(0,0).
\]
Equivalently, one must compute the actual microscopic projected tensor coefficients and confirm that they do not vanish by accidental cancellation or parameter tuning.

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetry allowance is automatic, actual witness nonvanishing is not.}
}
\]

\subsubsection{2. Actual realization of the minimal ansatz}

The minimal shell-enriched projector completion is a symmetry-compatible effective ansatz.
What is not yet proved is that the final microscopic TECT dynamics generates precisely this minimal operator structure with no additional symmetry-breaking first-order corrections.

Thus one must still verify that the actual microscopic linearization reduces to the same invariant basis
\[
B_\parallel,\quad B_I,\quad B_J
\]
with the same shell-relevant coupling pattern.

\subsubsection{3. Actual opposite-valley survival}

Within the minimal ansatz, opposite-valley matching is automatic.
However, in the final microscopic realization one must still verify that the reduced shell projection actually leaves a nontrivial surviving block at both \(+G_*\) and \(-G_*\).

So the remaining question is not whether matched opposite-valley pairing implies Dirac -- that is already closed.
The remaining question is whether the actual microscopic theory indeed realizes the two required shell blocks.

\subsubsection{4. Zero constant mixing in the actual remote-sector decomposition}

In the abstract theorem, if
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then
\[
V(0)=0.
\]
In the minimal truncation, the remote sectors were classified by shell-relevant labels, and this gave a sufficient sectorwise mismatch criterion.

What remains to be checked microscopically is that the actual remote-sector content of the final TECT truncation indeed shares no common shell-relevant irreducible component with the local Dirac block.

So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the zero-mixing theorem is closed, but the actual remote-sector irrep input must still be checked.}
}
\]

\subsubsection{5. Actual remote spectral gap}

The remote-gap problem has already been reduced to a finite Bloch-spectral inequality:
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Delta_\rho>0.
\]
However, the numerical or analytic value of \(\Delta_\rho\) depends on the actual microscopic truncation and has not yet been computed.

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the gap criterion is closed, but the actual gap value is not yet verified.}
}
\]

\subsubsection{6. Actual residual symmetry for mass protection}

The mass-protection problem is fully reduced to the finite check
\[
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\rho^1\otimes \mathbf 1,\,
\rho^2\otimes \mathbf 1
\}
=
\{0\}.
\]
A sufficient condition is preservation of valley-charge \(U(1)\).
What remains open is whether the actual microscopic TECT realization preserves such a symmetry, or an equivalent one, after all shell-enriched corrections are included.

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the mass-classification theorem is closed, but the actual residual symmetry algebra is not yet fixed.}
}
\]

\subsection{III. Final truth table}

We can now summarize the exact current logical status.

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|}
\hline
Statement & Minimal ansatz & Actual microscopic TECT \\
\hline
Finite-shell condensate PDE class & automatic & must be realized dynamically \\
\hline
Allowed tensor basis \(B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\) & automatic & must appear in actual linearization \\
\hline
Symmetry allowance of transverse channels & automatic & yes, inherited if same symmetry survives \\
\hline
Witness extraction formulas & automatic & automatic once the same shell basis is realized \\
\hline
Local Weyl criterion formula & automatic & automatic once actual witnesses are known \\
\hline
Opposite-valley witness matching & automatic & must verify actual \(-G_*\) block survives and matches \\
\hline
Zero-mixing theorem & automatic theorem & must verify actual irrep mismatch input \\
\hline
Remote-gap theorem & automatic theorem & must verify actual finite gap inequality \\
\hline
Mass-space classification & automatic theorem & must verify actual residual symmetry excludes masses \\
\hline
Stable massless local Dirac cone & conditional & requires all actual checks \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{IV. Precise current status}

The most honest global statement is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{At the minimal shell-enriched projector level, the local Weyl/Dirac architecture is essentially complete.}
}
\label{eq:minimal_complete}
\end{equation}

But:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{At the final microscopic TECT level, four explicit checks still remain:}
}
\label{eq:mic_checks}
\end{equation}
namely
\begin{enumerate}
\item actual witness nonvanishing,
\item actual opposite-valley survival,
\item actual remote gap,
\item actual residual symmetry excluding the two mass generators.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{V. Final theorem-level formulation}

We may summarize the situation in theorem form.

\begin{theorem}[Final separation theorem]
The following are fully closed at the level of the minimal shell-enriched projector ansatz:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-relevant invariant tensor basis;
\item the explicit witness extraction;
\item the local Weyl determinant formula;
\item the opposite-valley witness matching mechanism;
\item the zero-mixing theorem;
\item the remote-gap reduction theorem;
\item the mass-space classification theorem.
\end{enumerate}

The following are not yet automatic and must still be verified in the actual microscopic TECT realization:

\begin{enumerate}
\item actual nonvanishing of the positive and negative witness triples;
\item actual survival of the opposite shell valley;
\item actual irrep mismatch between the remote sector and the local Dirac block;
\item actual remote spectral gap;
\item actual residual symmetry forbidding the two intervalley mass matrices.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
All items in the first list were proved in the shell-reduced minimal ansatz by explicit invariant-basis construction, shell projection, opposite-valley matching, block decomposition, spectral reduction, and finite \(4\times4\) mass classification.
The second list consists precisely of the remaining input data required to transfer those abstract closed theorems into the final microscopic realization.
\end{proof}

\subsection{VI. Honest conclusion}

The correct final conclusion is not “the entire proof is finished,” but rather:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the theorem framework is finished, and the remaining work is explicit microscopic verification.}
}
\]

This is already a major achievement, because the unresolved part is no longer a conceptual uncertainty.
It is a finite checklist.

\section{Final Summary}

At the minimal shell-enriched projector level, the local fermion architecture is essentially closed.

Automatic in the minimal ansatz are:
\[
\text{the allowed tensor basis } \{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
\[
\text{the witness extraction formulas } (W_\parallel,W_I,W_J),
\]
\[
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
W_\parallel
\bigl(W_I^2+W_J^2\bigr),
\]
\[
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)=(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+),
\]
and the finite reduction of both the remote-gap problem and the mass-protection problem.

What is not yet automatic in the final microscopic TECT realization is:
\[
\text{actual witness nonvanishing},
\qquad
\text{actual opposite-valley survival},
\qquad
\text{actual remote spectral gap},
\qquad
\text{actual residual symmetry excluding the two mass matrices}.
\]

Therefore the present honest status is:
the theorem structure is finished, while the remaining work is an explicit finite microscopic verification program.
